</div>
			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">European migrant crisis</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arbeitsbesuch_Mazedonien_(20270359624).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Arbeitsbesuch_Mazedonien_%2820270359624%29.jpg/220px-Arbeitsbesuch_Mazedonien_%2820270359624%29.jpg" width="220" height="326" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Arbeitsbesuch_Mazedonien_%2820270359624%29.jpg/330px-Arbeitsbesuch_Mazedonien_%2820270359624%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Arbeitsbesuch_Mazedonien_%2820270359624%29.jpg/440px-Arbeitsbesuch_Mazedonien_%2820270359624%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2126" data-file-height="3151" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arbeitsbesuch_Mazedonien_(20270359624).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Migrants at the <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greek</a>–<a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Macedonian</a> border near <a href="/wiki/Gevgelija" title="Gevgelija">Gevgelija</a>, 24 August 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LE_Eithne_Operation_Triton.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/LE_Eithne_Operation_Triton.jpg/220px-LE_Eithne_Operation_Triton.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/LE_Eithne_Operation_Triton.jpg/330px-LE_Eithne_Operation_Triton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/LE_Eithne_Operation_Triton.jpg/440px-LE_Eithne_Operation_Triton.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3088" data-file-height="2056" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LE_Eithne_Operation_Triton.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Irish_Naval_Service" title="Irish Naval Service" class="mw-redirect">Irish Naval Service</a> rescuing migrants from an overcrowded boat as part of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Triton" title="Operation Triton">Operation Triton</a>, June 2015.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <b>European migrant crisis</b><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>n 1<span>]</span></a></sup> or <b>European refugee crisis</b><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>n 2<span>]</span></a></sup> arose through the rising number of <a href="/wiki/Refugees" title="Refugees" class="mw-redirect">refugees</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_migration" title="Human migration">migrants</a><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> coming to the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, across the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a> or through <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Europe" title="Southeast Europe">Southeast Europe</a>, and applying for <a href="/wiki/Right_of_asylum" title="Right of asylum">asylum</a>. They come from areas such as the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> (<a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>), <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gambia" title="Gambia" class="mw-redirect">Gambia</a>), and <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-origins_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-origins-13"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Balkans" title="Western Balkans" class="mw-redirect">Western Balkans</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_High_Commissioner_for_Refugees" title="United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees">United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees</a>, as of October 2015, the top three nationalities of the over half a million Mediterranean Sea arrivals since the beginning of the year are <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> (54%), <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> (15%) and <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a> (6%). Most of the refugees and migrants are adult men (68%).<sup id="cite_ref-:0_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-16"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> The phrase "European migrant crisis" became widely used in April 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> when five boats carrying almost two thousand <a href="/wiki/Human_migration" title="Human migration">migrants</a> to Europe <a href="/wiki/List_of_migrant_vessel_incidents_on_the_Mediterranean_Sea" title="List of migrant vessel incidents on the Mediterranean Sea">sank in the Mediterranean Sea</a>, with a combined death toll estimated at more than 1,200 people.</p>
<p>The shipwrecks took place in a context of ongoing conflicts and refugee crises in several Middle Eastern and African countries, as well as the refusal by several European Union governments to fund the Italian-run rescue option <a href="/wiki/Operation_Mare_Nostrum" title="Operation Mare Nostrum">Operation Mare Nostrum</a>, which was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Frontex" title="Frontex">Frontex</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Operation_Triton" title="Operation Triton">Operation Triton</a> in November 2014. Since April 2015, the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> has struggled to cope with the crisis, increasing funding for border patrol operations in the Mediterranean, devising plans to fight <a href="/wiki/Migrant_smuggling" title="Migrant smuggling" class="mw-redirect">migrant smuggling</a>, and proposing a new quota system to relocate and resettle asylum seekers among EU states and alleviate the burden on countries on the external borders of the Union. Individual countries have at times reintroduced border controls within the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>, and rifts have emerged between countries willing to accept asylum seekers and others trying to discourage their arrival.</p>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">EU member states</a> received 626,000 asylum applications in 2014, the highest number since the 672,000 applications received in 1992,<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-18"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> and granted protection status to more than 185,000 asylum seekers.<sup id="cite_ref-auto5_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto5-19"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Four states – Germany, Sweden, Italy and France – received around two-thirds of the EU's asylum applications and granted almost two-thirds of protection status in 2014; while Sweden, Hungary and Austria were among the top recipients of EU asylum applications <i>per capita</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto6_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto6-20"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto7_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto7-21"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> In the first half of 2015, EU member states received 395,000 new asylum applications.<sup id="cite_ref-asylumQ1_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asylumQ1-22"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-asylumQ2_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asylumQ2-23"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schengen_Area_and_Dublin_Regulation">Schengen Area and Dublin Regulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Schengen Area and Dublin Regulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_Schengen_Area.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Map_of_the_Schengen_Area.svg/250px-Map_of_the_Schengen_Area.svg.png" width="250" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Map_of_the_Schengen_Area.svg/375px-Map_of_the_Schengen_Area.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Map_of_the_Schengen_Area.svg/500px-Map_of_the_Schengen_Area.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1300" data-file-height="1300" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_Schengen_Area.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>, in blue</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Regulation" title="Dublin Regulation">Dublin Regulation</a></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen Agreement</a>, 26 European countries (22 of the 28 <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> member states, plus four <a href="/wiki/EFTA" title="EFTA" class="mw-redirect">EFTA</a> states) joined together to form an area, where border checks on internal Schengen borders (i. e. between member states) are abolished, and instead checks are restricted to the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area#Regulation_of_external_borders" title="Schengen Area">external Schengen borders</a> and countries with external borders are obligated to enforce border control regulations. Countries may reinstate internal border controls for a maximum of two months for “public policy or national security” reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Dublin_regulation" title="Dublin regulation" class="mw-redirect">Dublin regulation</a> determines the EU member state responsible to examine an <a href="/wiki/Right_of_asylum" title="Right of asylum">asylum</a> application to prevent asylum applicants in the EU from “<a href="/wiki/Asylum_shopping" title="Asylum shopping">asylum shopping</a>”, where applicants send applications for asylum to numerous EU member states, or “asylum orbiting”, where no member state takes responsibility for an asylum seeker. By default (when no family reasons or humanitarian grounds are present), the first member state that an asylum seeker entered and in which they have been fingerprinted is responsible. If the asylum seeker then moves to another member state, they can be transferred back to the member state they first entered. This has led many to criticise the Dublin rules for placing too much responsibility for asylum seekers on member states on the EU’s external borders (like Italy, Greece and Hungary), instead of devising a burden-sharing system among EU states.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics_on_the_EU.27s_foreign-born_population_prior_to_2015">Statistics on the EU's foreign-born population prior to 2015</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Statistics on the EU's foreign-born population prior to 2015">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Europe" title="Immigration to Europe">Immigration to Europe</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Immigration_in_the_EU.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Immigration_in_the_EU.png/300px-Immigration_in_the_EU.png" width="300" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Immigration_in_the_EU.png/450px-Immigration_in_the_EU.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Immigration_in_the_EU.png/600px-Immigration_in_the_EU.png 2x" data-file-width="837" data-file-height="556" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Immigration_in_the_EU.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Immigration of non-EU nationals (green),<sup id="cite_ref-Immigration_in_the_EU_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Immigration_in_the_EU-28"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> asylum applicants (orange)<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> and illegal border-crossings (blue)<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> in the European Union, 2010–2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Foreign_born" title="Foreign born">foreign-born</a> population residing in the EU in 2014 amounts to 33 million people, or 7% of the total population of the 28 EU countries (above 500 million people). By comparison, the foreign-born population is 1.63% of the total population in <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> 7.7% in <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> 13% in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, 20% in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> and 27% in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>. Between 2010 and 2013, around 1.4 million non-EU nationals, excluding asylum seekers and refugees, immigrated into the EU each year using regular means, with a slight decrease since 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-Immigration_in_the_EU_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Immigration_in_the_EU-28"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Prior to 2014, the number of asylum applications in the EU peaked in 1992 (672,000), 2001 (424,000) and 2013 (431,000). In 2014 it reached 626,000.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-18"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/UNHCR" title="UNHCR" class="mw-redirect">UNHCR</a>, the EU countries with the biggest numbers of recognized refugees at the end of 2014 were France (252,264), Germany (216,973), Sweden (142,207) and the United Kingdom (117,161). No European state was among the top ten refugee-hosting countries in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-UNHCRtrends_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCRtrends-33"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Prior to 2014, the number of <a href="/wiki/Illegal_entry" title="Illegal entry">illegal border crossings</a> detected by <a href="/wiki/Frontex" title="Frontex">Frontex</a> at the external borders of the EU peaked in 2011, with 141,051 sea and land irregular arrivals.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_refugee_crisis">Global refugee crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Global refugee crisis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Refugees_of_the_Syrian_Civil_War" title="Refugees of the Syrian Civil War">Refugees of the Syrian Civil War</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Top_countries_of_origin_and_asylum_of_refugees.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Top_countries_of_origin_and_asylum_of_refugees.svg/300px-Top_countries_of_origin_and_asylum_of_refugees.svg.png" width="300" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Top_countries_of_origin_and_asylum_of_refugees.svg/450px-Top_countries_of_origin_and_asylum_of_refugees.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Top_countries_of_origin_and_asylum_of_refugees.svg/600px-Top_countries_of_origin_and_asylum_of_refugees.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2590" data-file-height="1721" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Top_countries_of_origin_and_asylum_of_refugees.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Top ten countries of origin (red) and asylum (green) of refugees worldwide at the end of 2014, according to <a href="/wiki/UNHCR" title="UNHCR" class="mw-redirect">UNHCR</a> data (which exclude <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_refugees" title="Palestinian refugees" class="mw-redirect">Palestinian refugees</a> under <a href="/wiki/UNRWA" title="UNRWA">UNRWA</a> mandate).<sup id="cite_ref-UNHCRtrends_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCRtrends-33"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/UNHCR" title="UNHCR" class="mw-redirect">UNHCR</a>, the number of <a href="/wiki/Displaced_person" title="Displaced person">forcibly displaced people</a> worldwide reached 59.5 million at the end of 2014, the highest level since World War II,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> with a 40% increase taking place since 2011. Of these 59.5 million, 19.5 million were <a href="/wiki/Refugees" title="Refugees" class="mw-redirect">refugees</a> (14.4 million under UNHCR's mandate, plus 5.1 million <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_refugees" title="Palestinian refugees" class="mw-redirect">Palestinian refugees</a> under <a href="/wiki/UNRWA" title="UNRWA">UNRWA</a>'s mandate), and 1.8 million were <a href="/wiki/Asylum-seekers" title="Asylum-seekers" class="mw-redirect">asylum-seekers</a>. The rest were persons displaced within their own countries (<a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_persons" title="Internally displaced persons" class="mw-redirect">internally displaced persons</a>). The 14.4 million refugees under UNHCR's mandate were around 2.7 million more than at the end of 2013 (+23%), the highest level since 1995. Among them, <a href="/wiki/Syrian_refugees" title="Syrian refugees" class="mw-redirect">Syrian refugees</a> became the largest refugee group in 2014 (3.9 million, 1.55 million more than the previous year), overtaking <a href="/wiki/Afghan_refugees" title="Afghan refugees">Afghan refugees</a> (2.6 million), who had been the largest refugee group for three decades. Six of the ten largest countries of origin of refugees were African: <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sudanese_refugees" title="Sudanese refugees" class="mw-redirect">Sudan</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of Congo" class="mw-redirect">Democratic Republic of Congo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UNHCRtrends_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCRtrends-33"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Developing_countries" title="Developing countries" class="mw-redirect">Developing countries</a> hosted the largest share of refugees (86% by the end of 2014, the highest figure in more than two decades); the <a href="/wiki/Least_developed_countries" title="Least developed countries" class="mw-redirect">least developed countries</a> alone provided asylum to 25% of refugees worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-UNHCRtrends_33-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCRtrends-33"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Even though most Syrian refugees were hosted by neighbouring countries such as <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, the number of Syrian refugees applying for asylum in Europe steadily increased between 2011 and 2015, totalling 428,735 in 37 European countries (including both EU members and non-members) as of the end of August 2015; 43% of them applied for asylum in <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> or <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> The largest single recipient of new <a href="/wiki/Asylum_seekers" title="Asylum seekers" class="mw-redirect">asylum seekers</a> worldwide in 2014 was the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" title="Russian Federation" class="mw-redirect">Russian Federation</a>, with 274,700 asylum requests, 99% of them lodged by <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians" title="Ukrainians">Ukrainians</a> fleeing from the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Donbass" title="War in Donbass">war in Donbass</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-UNHCRtrends_33-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCRtrends-33"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Russia was followed by Germany, the top recipient of asylum applications within the European Union, with 202,645 asylum requests, 20% of them from Syria.<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-18"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beginning_of_the_European_crisis">Beginning of the European crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Beginning of the European crisis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Libyan_Crisis" title="Libyan Crisis" class="mw-redirect">Libyan Crisis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Operation_Mare_Nostrum" title="Operation Mare Nostrum">Operation Mare Nostrum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Operation_Triton" title="Operation Triton">Operation Triton</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Greek_Turkish_Bulgarian_borders_and_maritsa_river.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Greek_Turkish_Bulgarian_borders_and_maritsa_river.svg/300px-Greek_Turkish_Bulgarian_borders_and_maritsa_river.svg.png" width="300" height="351" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Greek_Turkish_Bulgarian_borders_and_maritsa_river.svg/450px-Greek_Turkish_Bulgarian_borders_and_maritsa_river.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Greek_Turkish_Bulgarian_borders_and_maritsa_river.svg/600px-Greek_Turkish_Bulgarian_borders_and_maritsa_river.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="599" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Greek_Turkish_Bulgarian_borders_and_maritsa_river.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Greek, Turkish, and Bulgarian borders and the course of the Maritsa River</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Between 2007 and 2011, large numbers of undocumented migrants from the Middle East and Africa crossed between Turkey and Greece, leading Greece and the European Border Protection agency Frontex to upgrade border controls.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcsep2014_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcsep2014-38"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, immigrant influx into Greece by land decreased by 95% after the construction of a fence on that part of the Greek–Turkish frontier which does not follow the course of the <a href="/wiki/Maritsa" title="Maritsa">Maritsa</a> River.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2015, Bulgaria followed by upgrading a border fence to prevent migrant flows through Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Minat_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minat-41"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Instability and the <a href="/wiki/Libyan_Civil_War_(2014%E2%80%93present)" title="Libyan Civil War (2014–present)">second civil war in Libya</a> have made departures easier from the north-African country, with no central authority controlling Libya’s ports and dealing with European countries, and <a href="/wiki/Migrant_smuggling" title="Migrant smuggling" class="mw-redirect">migrant smuggling</a> networks flourishing. The war could also have forced to leave many African immigrants residing in Libya, which used to be itself a destination country for migrants looking for better jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2013_Lampedusa_migrant_shipwreck" title="2013 Lampedusa migrant shipwreck">2013 Lampedusa migrant shipwreck</a> involved "more than 360" deaths, leading the Italian government to establish <a href="/wiki/Operation_Mare_Nostrum" title="Operation Mare Nostrum">Operation Mare Nostrum</a>, a large-scale naval operation that involved <a href="/wiki/Search_and_rescue" title="Search and rescue">search and rescue</a>, with some migrants brought aboard a naval <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_assault_ship" title="Amphibious assault ship">amphibious assault ship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2014, the Italian government ended the operation, citing costs to be too large for one EU state alone to manage; Frontex assumed the main responsibility for search and rescue operations. The Frontex operation is called <a href="/wiki/Operation_Triton" title="Operation Triton">Operation Triton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-European_Commission_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-European_Commission-44"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> The Italian government had requested additional funds from the EU to continue the operation but member states did not offer the requested support.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> The UK government cited fears that the operation was acting as "an unintended 'pull factor', encouraging more migrants to attempt the dangerous sea crossing and thereby leading to more tragic and unnecessary deaths".<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> The operation consists of two surveillance aircraft and three ships, with seven teams of staff who gather intelligence and conduct screening/identification processing. Its monthly budget is estimated at €2.9&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-European_Commission_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-European_Commission-44"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Migration">Migration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Migration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Statistics">Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sea_and_land_arrivals_to_the_EU">Sea and land arrivals to the EU</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Sea and land arrivals to the EU">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Flag_of_Somalia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Somalia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Flag_of_Somalia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Somalia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Flag_of_Somalia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Somalia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a></td>
<td>7,676</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Others</td>
<td>54,216</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><b>Total</b></td>
<td><b>283,532</b></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Migration" title="International Organization for Migration">International Organization for Migration</a>, up to 3,072 people died or disappeared in 2014 in the Mediterranean while trying to migrate to Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-48"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Overall estimates are that over 22,000 migrants died between 2000 and 2014.</p>
<p>In 2014, 283,532 migrants illegally<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Disputed statement" class="mw-redirect"><span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (October 2015)">dubious</span></a> <span class="metadata">– <a href="/wiki/Talk:European_migrant_crisis#Dubious" title="Talk:European migrant crisis">discuss</a></span></i>]</sup> entered the European Union, mainly following the Central Mediterranean, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Mediterranean" title="Eastern Mediterranean">Eastern Mediterranean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Balkans" title="Western Balkans" class="mw-redirect">Western Balkan</a> routes.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-48"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> 220,194 migrants crossed EU sea borders in the Central, Eastern and Western Mediterranean (a 266% increase compared to 2013). Half of them had come from Syria, Eritrea and Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-FrontexARA2015_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FrontexARA2015-47"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Of those arriving in Southern Europe in 2014, the vast majority (170,664, a 277% increase compared to 2013) arrived in Italy through Libya, whereas a minority (50,834, a 105% increase) arrived in Greece through Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> 62,000 applied for <a href="/wiki/Right_of_asylum" title="Right of asylum">asylum</a> in Italy, but most Syrians and Eritreans, who comprised almost half of the arrivals in Italy in 2014, didn’t stop in Italy, and continued their journey towards northern Europe, Germany and Sweden in particular.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, a shift took place, with Greece overtaking Italy as the primary point of arrival and surpassing in the first six months of 2015 the numbers for the whole of 2014: 67,500 people arrived in Italy, mainly coming from <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a> (25%), <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> (10%) and <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> (10%), whereas 68,000 arrived on the islands of Greece, mainly coming from <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> (57%) and <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> (22%).<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> In total, 137,000 migrants crossed the Mediterranean into Europe in the first six months of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-MediterraneanCrisis2015_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MediterraneanCrisis2015-54"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As of 17 April 2015, the total number of migrants reaching the Italian coasts was 21,191 since 1 January 2015, with a decrease during the month of March due to bad weather conditions, and a surge since 10 April, bringing the total number of arrivals in line with the number recorded in the same period in 2014. However, the death toll in the first four months of 2014 was 96, compared with 500 in the same period in 2015; this number excluded the victims of the devastating shipwrecks on 13 and 19 April.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In early August 2015, the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees said that 250,000 migrants had arrived in Europe by sea so far in 2015, 124,000 in Greece and 98,000 in Italy.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCnavyrescues_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCnavyrescues-57"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Frontex" title="Frontex">Frontex</a>, July set a new record for a single month, with 107,500 migrants estimated to have entered the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-JulySetsRecord_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JulySetsRecord-58"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> 190,000 people were detected crossing the EU borders in August and a further 170,000 in September, bringing the number of migrants detected at EU external borders in the first nine months of the year to 710,000 (350,000 in Greece, 129,000 in Italy and 204,000 in Hungary, although a large number of migrants following the Western Balkan route were double-counted when arriving in Greece and then when entering the EU for the second time through Hungary or Croatia).<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Migration" title="International Organization for Migration">IOM</a> estimates, 432,761 migrants and refugees had reached Europe by sea as of 10 September 2015, almost double the amount of arrivals in the Mediterranean for the entire 2014. 70% of all 2015 arrivals were registered in Greece (309,356) and 28% in Italy (the number of arrivals in Italy, 121,139, remained stable in comparison to the same period the previous year). Over 70% of the arrivals in Greece came from Syria. IOM estimated that a total of 2,748 migrants had lost their lives in the Mediterranean so far in 2015, of which 2,620 in the Central Mediterranean route, although it noted that the expansion of the Frontex <a href="/wiki/Operation_Triton" title="Operation Triton">Operation Triton</a> in the Mediterranean had decreased somewhat the mortality rate in the last few months.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Asylum_applications">Asylum applications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Asylum applications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_European_Migrant_Crisis_2015.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Map_of_the_European_Migrant_Crisis_2015.png/300px-Map_of_the_European_Migrant_Crisis_2015.png" width="300" height="279" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Map_of_the_European_Migrant_Crisis_2015.png/450px-Map_of_the_European_Migrant_Crisis_2015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Map_of_the_European_Migrant_Crisis_2015.png/600px-Map_of_the_European_Migrant_Crisis_2015.png 2x" data-file-width="2192" data-file-height="2040" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_European_Migrant_Crisis_2015.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Asylum applications in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Free_Trade_Association" title="European Free Trade Association">EFTA</a> States between 1 January and 30 June 2015 according to <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a> data.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_European_Migrant_Crisis_2015_-_Asylum_applicants%27_countries_of_origin.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Map_of_the_European_Migrant_Crisis_2015_-_Asylum_applicants%27_countries_of_origin.png/300px-Map_of_the_European_Migrant_Crisis_2015_-_Asylum_applicants%27_countries_of_origin.png" width="300" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Map_of_the_European_Migrant_Crisis_2015_-_Asylum_applicants%27_countries_of_origin.png/450px-Map_of_the_European_Migrant_Crisis_2015_-_Asylum_applicants%27_countries_of_origin.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Map_of_the_European_Migrant_Crisis_2015_-_Asylum_applicants%27_countries_of_origin.png/600px-Map_of_the_European_Migrant_Crisis_2015_-_Asylum_applicants%27_countries_of_origin.png 2x" data-file-width="2519" data-file-height="1539" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_European_Migrant_Crisis_2015_-_Asylum_applicants%27_countries_of_origin.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Countries of origin of asylum applicants in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Free_Trade_Association" title="European Free Trade Association">EFTA</a> States between 1 January and 30 June 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union" title="Member state of the European Union">EU member states</a> received 626,715 asylum applications in 2014, the highest number since the 672,000 applications received in 1992. The main countries of origin of asylum seekers, accounting for almost half of the total, were <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> (20%), <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> (7%), <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> (6%), <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a> (6%) and <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> (5%).<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto2-18"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, decisions on asylum applications in the EU made at the first instance resulted in more than 160,000 asylum seekers being granted protection status, while a further 23,000 received protection status on appeal. The rate of recognition of asylum applicants was 45% at the first instance and 18% on appeal. The main beneficiaries of protection status, accounting for more than half of the total, were Syrians (68,300 or 37%), Eritreans (14,600 or 8%) and Afghanis (14,100 or 8%).<sup id="cite_ref-auto5_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto5-19"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Four states – Germany, Sweden, Italy and France – received around two-thirds of the EU's asylum applications and granted almost two-thirds of protection status in 2014. Sweden, Hungary and Austria were among the top recipients of EU asylum applications <i>per capita</i>, when adjusted for their own populations, with 8.4 asylum seekers per 1,000 inhabitants in Sweden, 4.3 in Hungary and 3.2 in Austria.<sup id="cite_ref-auto6_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto6-20"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto7_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto7-21"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In the first three months of 2015, the number of new asylum applicants in the EU was 184,800, increasing by 86% if compared with the same quarter in the previous year but remaining stable if compared to the last quarter of 2014. More than half applied for asylum in Germany (40%) or Hungary (18%). The main nationalities of the applicants were Kosovo (48,875 or 26%), Syria (29,100 or 16%) and Afghanistan (12,910 or 7%).<sup id="cite_ref-asylumQ1_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asylumQ1-22"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> In the second quarter of 2015, 213,200 people applied for asylum in the EU, up by 15% compared with the previous quarter. 38% applied for asylum in Germany, followed by Hungary (15%) and Austria (8%). The main countries of citizenship of asylum seekers, accounting for more than half of the total, were Syria (21%), Afghanistan (13%), Albania (8%), Iraq (6%) and Kosovo (5%).<sup id="cite_ref-asylumQ2_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asylumQ2-23"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Asylum_quarterly_report_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asylum_quarterly_report-63"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> In August 2015, the German government announced that it expects to receive 800,000 asylum applications by the end of the year, more than the whole EU in 2014. Until July 2015, Syrian refugees were the biggest group of asylum seekers in Germany, with 44,417 applications lodged since January, whereas 40% of applications came from people from the Balkans, who were thought not to qualify for asylum for the most part.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins_and_motivations">Origins and motivations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Origins and motivations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ascertaining motivation is complex, but most of the migrants are <a href="/wiki/Refugees" title="Refugees" class="mw-redirect">refugees</a>, fleeing war and <a href="/wiki/Persecution" title="Persecution">persecution</a> in countries such as <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a>: according to <a href="/wiki/UNHCR" title="UNHCR" class="mw-redirect">UNHCR</a> data, as of October 2015, 83% of Mediterranean Sea arrivals come from the world's top ten refugee-producing countries (54% from Syria, 15% from Afghanistan, 6% from Eritrea, 4% from <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, 2% from <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> and 1% from <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>). The top ten nationalities of Mediterranean Sea arrivals also include <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> (3%), <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> (2%), <a href="/wiki/Gambia" title="Gambia" class="mw-redirect">Gambia</a> (1%) and <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> (1%).<sup id="cite_ref-:0_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-16"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNHCRtrends_33-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCRtrends-33"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Asylum seekers of seven nationalities had an asylum recognition rate of over 50% in EU States in the first quarter of 2015, meaning that they obtained protection over half the time they applied: Syrians (94% recognition rate), Eritreans (90%), <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraqis</a> (88%), Afghans (66%), <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iranians</a> (65%), <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalis</a> (60%) and <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudanese</a> (53%). Migrants of these nationalities accounted for 90% of the arrivals in Greece and 47% of the arrivals in Italy between January and August 2015, according to UNHCR data.<sup id="cite_ref-Asylum_quarterly_report_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asylum_quarterly_report-63"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> Wars fueling the crisis are the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_civil_war" title="Syrian civil war" class="mw-redirect">Syrian civil war</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War_(2014%E2%80%93present)" title="Iraq War (2014–present)" class="mw-redirect">Iraq war</a>, the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)" class="mw-redirect">war in Afghanistan</a>, the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Somalia_(2009%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Somalia (2009–present)">war in Somalia</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Darfur" title="War in Darfur">war in Darfur</a>. Refugees from <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a>, one of the <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Eritrea" title="Human rights in Eritrea">most repressive</a> states in the world, flee from indefinite military <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscription</a> and <a href="/wiki/Forced_labour" title="Forced labour" class="mw-redirect">forced labour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-origins_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-origins-13"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Migrants from the <a href="/wiki/Western_Balkans" title="Western Balkans" class="mw-redirect">Western Balkans</a> (<a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>) and parts of <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a> (Gambia, Nigeria) and <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a> (Bangladesh, Pakistan) are more likely to be <a href="/wiki/Economic_migrants" title="Economic migrants" class="mw-redirect">economic migrants</a>, fleeing poverty and lack of jobs, many of them hoping for a better lifestyle and job offers, without valid claims to <a href="/wiki/Convention_relating_to_the_Status_of_Refugees" title="Convention relating to the Status of Refugees">refugee status</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NossiterNiger_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NossiterNiger-68"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-smh.com.au_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-smh.com.au-69"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> The influx from states like <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> is mixed, made up in part of refugees fleeing from violence and war (like the <a href="/wiki/Boko_Haram_insurgency" title="Boko Haram insurgency">Boko Haram insurgency</a> in north-east Nigeria and the <a href="/wiki/War_in_North-West_Pakistan" title="War in North-West Pakistan">war in North-West Pakistan</a>), in part of economic migrants.<sup id="cite_ref-origins_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-origins-13"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Refugees and migrants have been seeking to settle preferentially in those national destinations offering more generous <a href="/wiki/Social_welfare" title="Social welfare" class="mw-redirect">social welfare</a> benefits and hosting more established Middle Eastern and African immigrant communities.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> In contrast to Germany, historically a popular final destination for the EU migrants, France saw its popularity erode in 2015 among migrants seeking asylum.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> Motivations for migrant smugglers are primarily financial, proving highly lucrative for many.<sup id="cite_ref-MigrantsTurkey_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MigrantsTurkey-75"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> Europe has also received a record number of asylum applications from child refugees in 2015, as younger refugees are perceived as being more likely to receive asylum per request.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Migrant_routes">Migrant routes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Migrant routes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of August 2015, <a href="/wiki/Frontex" title="Frontex">Frontex</a> recognizes the following general routes on sea and on land used by irregular migrants to enter the EU:<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Migrants_in_Hungary_2015_Aug_003.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Migrants_in_Hungary_2015_Aug_003.jpg/220px-Migrants_in_Hungary_2015_Aug_003.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Migrants_in_Hungary_2015_Aug_003.jpg/330px-Migrants_in_Hungary_2015_Aug_003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Migrants_in_Hungary_2015_Aug_003.jpg/440px-Migrants_in_Hungary_2015_Aug_003.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Migrants_in_Hungary_2015_Aug_003.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Migrants along the Balkan route crossing from Serbia into Hungary, 24 August 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>the Western African route</li>
<li>the Western Mediterranean route</li>
<li>the Central Mediterranean route</li>
<li>the <a href="/wiki/Apulia" title="Apulia">Apulia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Calabria" title="Calabria">Calabria</a> route</li>
<li>the circular route from Albania to Greece</li>
<li>the Western Balkan route (from Greece through Macedonia and Serbia to <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> or <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-aljazeera.com_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera.com-78"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>the Eastern Mediterranean route</li>
<li>the Eastern Borders route</li>
</ul>
<p>In addition, an Arctic route had emerged by September 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-ArcticRoute_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ArcticRoute-79"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkey">Turkey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Turkey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The vast majority of migrants and refugees entering Europe by sea in 2015, nearly half million by September, arrived from Turkey, according to the United Nations.<sup id="cite_ref-MigrantsTurkey_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MigrantsTurkey-75"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> Turkish officials attempting to deter migration facilitated by smugglers have detained 57,000 travelers and over 100 human traffickers in 2015 through September.<sup id="cite_ref-MigrantsTurkey_75-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MigrantsTurkey-75"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Malta">Malta</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Malta">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Distressed_persons_are_transferred_to_a_Maltese_patrol_vessel..jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Distressed_persons_are_transferred_to_a_Maltese_patrol_vessel..jpg/220px-Distressed_persons_are_transferred_to_a_Maltese_patrol_vessel..jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Distressed_persons_are_transferred_to_a_Maltese_patrol_vessel..jpg/330px-Distressed_persons_are_transferred_to_a_Maltese_patrol_vessel..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Distressed_persons_are_transferred_to_a_Maltese_patrol_vessel..jpg/440px-Distressed_persons_are_transferred_to_a_Maltese_patrol_vessel..jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Distressed_persons_are_transferred_to_a_Maltese_patrol_vessel..jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rescued migrants near Malta, October 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Malta#Immigration" title="Demographics of Malta">Demographics of Malta § Immigration</a></div>
<p>Between 2008 and 2012, Malta received on average the highest number of <a href="/wiki/Asylum_seekers" title="Asylum seekers" class="mw-redirect">asylum seekers</a> compared to its national population: 21.7 applicants per 1,000 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, most of these asylum applications were submitted by nationals of <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, more than half of the requests were by <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalian</a> nationals alone.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> In a 2013 news story, <i>The Guardian</i> reported, "Before Malta joined the EU in 2004, immigration levels were negligible. Because it is located close to north Africa, it has now become a gateway for migrants seeking entry to Europe."<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, very few migrants arrived in Malta compared to previous years, since most of those rescued were taken to <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>. In September, 78 migrants rescued by the <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Malta" title="Armed Forces of Malta">Armed Forces of Malta</a> refused to be brought to Malta.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> They insisted on going to Italy, and were eventually taken there.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Melilla_and_Ceuta_.28Spain.29">Melilla and Ceuta (Spain)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Melilla and Ceuta (Spain)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Ambox_current_red.svg" class="image"><img alt="Ambox current red.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Ambox_current_red.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></a></div>
</td>

</tr>
</table>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Verjamelilla.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Verjamelilla.jpg/220px-Verjamelilla.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Verjamelilla.jpg/330px-Verjamelilla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Verjamelilla.jpg/440px-Verjamelilla.jpg 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="675" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Verjamelilla.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Melilla_border_fence" title="Melilla border fence">Melilla border fence</a> In <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Melilla_border_fence" title="Melilla border fence">Melilla border fence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ceuta_border_fence" title="Ceuta border fence">Ceuta border fence</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Melilla" title="Melilla">Melilla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a>, two autonomous Spanish cities on the north coast of Africa bordering <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, are the only EU territories to share a land border with Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> The number of undocumented migrants hoping to reach the EU via Melilla or Ceuta grew in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lampedusa_.28Italy.29">Lampedusa (Italy)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Lampedusa (Italy)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lampedusa_immigrant_reception_center" title="Lampedusa immigrant reception center">Lampedusa immigrant reception center</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pelagie_Islands_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Pelagie_Islands_map.png/220px-Pelagie_Islands_map.png" width="220" height="260" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Pelagie_Islands_map.png/330px-Pelagie_Islands_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Pelagie_Islands_map.png/440px-Pelagie_Islands_map.png 2x" data-file-width="596" data-file-height="705" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pelagie_Islands_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Location of <a href="/wiki/Lampedusa" title="Lampedusa">Lampedusa</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Migranti_sbarcati_in_Italia_1997-2014.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Migranti_sbarcati_in_Italia_1997-2014.png/220px-Migranti_sbarcati_in_Italia_1997-2014.png" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Migranti_sbarcati_in_Italia_1997-2014.png/330px-Migranti_sbarcati_in_Italia_1997-2014.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Migranti_sbarcati_in_Italia_1997-2014.png/440px-Migranti_sbarcati_in_Italia_1997-2014.png 2x" data-file-width="903" data-file-height="558" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Migranti_sbarcati_in_Italia_1997-2014.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Migrants arrived in Italy by sea, 1997–2014<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Thousands of migrants have been trying every month to cross the Mediterranean to Europe, risking their lives on unsafe boats including fishing trawlers.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> Many of them are fleeing poverty-stricken homelands or war-torn countries and seeking economic opportunity within the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-Boatsform_Libya_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boatsform_Libya-90"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> Italy, and, in particular, its southern island of <a href="/wiki/Lampedusa" title="Lampedusa">Lampedusa</a>, receives enormous numbers of Africans and Middle-Easterners transported by traffickers operating along the ungoverned coast of the <a href="/wiki/Failed_state" title="Failed state">failed state</a> of Libya.<sup id="cite_ref-Boatsform_Libya_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boatsform_Libya-90"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MappingBBC_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MappingBBC-92"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2013, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Pope Francis</a> visited the island on his first official visit outside of Rome. He prayed for migrants, living and dead, and denounced their traffickers.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> In October 2013, <a href="/wiki/2013_Lampedusa_migrant_shipwreck" title="2013 Lampedusa migrant shipwreck">a disaster</a> occurred; a boat carrying over 500 migrants, mostly from <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, sank off the coast of Lampedusa with the deaths of at least 300 people.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_24456058_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_24456058-94"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a>'s regional parliament has declared a state of emergency.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, 170,100 migrants arrived in Italy by sea, a 296% increase compared to 2013. 141,484 of the travelers ferried over from Libya. Most of the migrants had come from <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, Eritrea and various countries in <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>From January to April 2015, about 1600 migrants died on the route from Libya to Lampedusa, making it the deadliest migrant route in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Greece">Greece</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Greece">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aegean_Sea_with_island_groups_labeled.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Aegean_Sea_with_island_groups_labeled.gif/220px-Aegean_Sea_with_island_groups_labeled.gif" width="220" height="292" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Aegean_Sea_with_island_groups_labeled.gif/330px-Aegean_Sea_with_island_groups_labeled.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fb/Aegean_Sea_with_island_groups_labeled.gif 2x" data-file-width="350" data-file-height="465" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aegean_Sea_with_island_groups_labeled.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Island groups of the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Migrants arrive from the Middle East making the 6-kilometre (4&#160;mi) water crossing to the <a href="/wiki/Greek_islands" title="Greek islands" class="mw-redirect">Greek islands</a> of <a href="/wiki/Chios" title="Chios">Chios</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kos" title="Kos">Kos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lesbos" title="Lesbos">Lesbos</a>, which are close to Turkey and are thus a quick and easy access border into Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Yeginsu_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yeginsu-99"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Neely_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neely-100"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Daley_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daley-101"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite being a member country, Greece gave up on fulfilling its <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area#Regulation_of_external_borders" title="Schengen Area">external Schengen borders</a> to try to stop and register migrants. The French honorary consul in the Turkish port of <a href="/wiki/Bodrum" title="Bodrum">Bodrum</a>, who sold boats to migrants, claimed that local <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkish authorities</a> have been also involved in human trafficking.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2015, 124,000 people had arrived, a 750% increase from 2014, mainly stemming from the wars in Syria, Iraq and Afghanistan. Greece appealed to the European Union for assistance, whilst the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Commission_on_Human_Rights" title="United Nations Commission on Human Rights">UNCHR</a> European Director Vincent Cochetel said facilities for the refugees on the Greek islands were "totally inadequate" and the islands in "total chaos".<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Frontex's Operation Poseidon, aimed at patrolling the <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Sea" title="Aegean Sea">Aegean Sea</a>, is badly underfunded and undermanned, with only 11 coastal patrol vessels, one ship, two helicopters, two aircraft and a budget of €18 million.<sup id="cite_ref-PopFrontexGreece_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PopFrontexGreece-104"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Human traffickers charge illegal immigrants $1,000 to $1,500 for the 25-minute boat ride from <a href="/wiki/Bodrum" title="Bodrum">Bodrum</a>, Turkey to Kos.<sup id="cite_ref-Yeginsu_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yeginsu-99"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> In August 2015, "hundreds" of boats made the crossing carrying illegal immigrants every night.<sup id="cite_ref-Yeginsu_99-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yeginsu-99"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> The migrants, many of them with cell phones and smart phones and detailed knowledge of illegal routes across Europe, travel onward to <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki" title="Thessaloniki">Thessaloniki</a> in the mainland of Greece and estimate that it will cost them €3,000 to €4,000 to reach Germany, and €10,000 or €12,000 to reach Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-Yeginsu_99-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yeginsu-99"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> Desperate migrants have fought brawls over places in boats leaving Bodrum for Kos.<sup id="cite_ref-KilledbyFumes_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KilledbyFumes-105"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2015, the photos of dead 3-year-old <a href="/wiki/Alan_Kurdi" title="Alan Kurdi" class="mw-redirect">Alan Kurdi</a>, who drowned when he and his family were in a small inflatable boat which capsized shortly after leaving Bodrum trying to reach the Greek island of Kos, made headlines around the world. Konstantinos Vardakis, the top EU diplomat in <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>, told <i>The New York Times</i> that at least 250 Iraqis per day had been landing on Greek islands between mid-August and early September 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hungary">Hungary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Hungary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Number_of_migrants_in_Hungary_per_week.pdf" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Number_of_migrants_in_Hungary_per_week.pdf/page1-220px-Number_of_migrants_in_Hungary_per_week.pdf.jpg" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Number_of_migrants_in_Hungary_per_week.pdf/page1-330px-Number_of_migrants_in_Hungary_per_week.pdf.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Number_of_migrants_in_Hungary_per_week.pdf/page1-440px-Number_of_migrants_in_Hungary_per_week.pdf.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1754" data-file-height="1239" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Number_of_migrants_in_Hungary_per_week.pdf" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Number of migrants in Hungary per week, May–September 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hungary%E2%80%93Serbia_border_fence" title="Hungary–Serbia border fence" class="mw-redirect">Hungary–Serbia border fence</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hungarian-Serbian_border_barrier_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Hungarian-Serbian_border_barrier_1.jpg/220px-Hungarian-Serbian_border_barrier_1.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Hungarian-Serbian_border_barrier_1.jpg/330px-Hungarian-Serbian_border_barrier_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Hungarian-Serbian_border_barrier_1.jpg/440px-Hungarian-Serbian_border_barrier_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="850" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hungarian-Serbian_border_barrier_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Hungary%E2%80%93Serbia_border_fence" title="Hungary–Serbia border fence" class="mw-redirect">Hungarian–Serbian border fence</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Refugee_march_Hungary_2015-09-04_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Refugee_march_Hungary_2015-09-04_02.jpg/220px-Refugee_march_Hungary_2015-09-04_02.jpg" width="220" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Refugee_march_Hungary_2015-09-04_02.jpg/330px-Refugee_march_Hungary_2015-09-04_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Refugee_march_Hungary_2015-09-04_02.jpg/440px-Refugee_march_Hungary_2015-09-04_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3135" data-file-height="1674" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Refugee_march_Hungary_2015-09-04_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Migrants in Hungary on their march towards <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Migrants taking the Balkans route cross into the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a> first in Greece. Despite Schengen obligations, Greece does not try to stop and register them. Migrants enter the Schengen Area again on the Serbian–Hungarian border. In June 2015, Hungary said it was contemplating countermeasures against the influx of illegal immigrants from Serbia, a non-EU and non-Schengen state.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 17 June 2015, the Hungarian government announced the construction of a 4-metre-high (13&#160;ft), 175-kilometre-long (109&#160;mi) fence along its southern border with Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> Although Hungary acted in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen Agreement</a> that obligates countries with <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area#Regulation_of_external_borders" title="Schengen Area">external Schengen borders</a> to protect it from illegal crossing and exercise border checks, the <a href="/wiki/European_Comission" title="European Comission" class="mw-redirect">European Comission</a> warned EU members against steps that contravene EU obligations and urging members like Hungary to find other ways to cope with an inflow of illegal migrants.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> The first phase of the construction was finished at the end of August and Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Orb%C3%A1n" title="Viktor Orbán">Viktor Orbán</a> announced that it would be fully completed by the end of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 3 September 2015, Hungary's prime minister, Viktor Orbán, defended the country's management of the migrant situation internally, notwithstanding chaos at Budapest's <a href="/wiki/Budapest_Keleti_railway_station" title="Budapest Keleti railway station">main international rail station</a>, while criticising Germany and Europe overall for not dissuading migrants from entering Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> On the same day, Hungarian police let migrants board a train in Budapest heading west, then stopped it in <a href="/wiki/Bicske" title="Bicske">Bicske</a> and tried to transport migrants to a registration camp there. The migrants refused to cooperate and remained on the train, which did not travel further west.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 4 September 2015, about a thousand of the migrants at Railway Station East (Keleti Pályaudvar) set off by foot toward Austria and Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> On the same night, the Hungarian government decided to send buses to transport illegal migrants to <a href="/wiki/Hegyeshalom" title="Hegyeshalom">Hegyeshalom</a>, on the border with Austria.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
