<p>On 14 September 2015, it was reported that the Hungarian police was blocking the route from Serbia, and that the regular entry-point was heavily manned with officers, soldiers and helicopters hovering above,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> sealing this border with a razor wire<sup id="cite_ref-Wire1_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wire1-118"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wire2_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wire2-119"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> and detaining migrants crossing the border illegally as of 12 am on 15 September 2015 with the threat of arrest and criminal charges.<sup id="cite_ref-Wire2_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wire2-119"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> On the Hungarian side, volunteers were seen giving handouts showing a map with alternate routes through Croatia marked, created by the administrators of the <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> group "Avoid Hungary – Migration news". This has, in turn, resulted in Croatian Facebook commenters urging the migrants to be careful when crossing the <a href="/wiki/Croatia%E2%80%93Serbia_border_dispute" title="Croatia–Serbia border dispute">Croatia–Serbia border</a>, due to a large number of still active <a href="/wiki/Landmines" title="Landmines" class="mw-redirect">landmines</a> not yet removed since the 1990s' <a href="/wiki/Croatian_War_of_Independence" title="Croatian War of Independence">War of Independence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> Meanwhile, on 15 September 2015, Hungary sealed its border with Serbia. Several hundred migrants broke the fence between Hungary and Serbia twice on Wednesday, 16 September, and threw chunks of concrete and water bottles over the fence. Hungarian police reacted with tear gas and water cannons at <a href="/wiki/Horgo%C5%A1" title="Horgoš">Horgoš</a> 2 border crossing. <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">Belgrade</a> protested these actions but the Serbian police did nothing to stop the violence. A 20-year-old Iraqi refugee has been sentenced to deportation and one-year entry ban in Hungary, as well as €80 in court fees, according to the new law put into action a few days ago.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> On 18 September, Hungary started building another fence, this time along the border with Croatia, a fellow EU member state, but not part of the Schengen Area.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> Within two weeks tens of thousands of refugees crossed from Croatia to Hungary, most of which went towards the Austrian border <sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 16 October 2015, Hungary announced that it would close its border with Croatia to migrants,<sup id="cite_ref-HungaryCroatia2_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HungaryCroatia2-124"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> and since 17 October onward, thousands of migrants daily were diverted to Slovenia instead.<sup id="cite_ref-SloveniaCroatia2_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SloveniaCroatia2-125"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Croatia">Croatia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Croatia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NE_PRILAZITE_-_NA_OVOM_PODRUCJU_JE_VELIKA_OPASNOST_OD_MINA_(Hrvatska,_7_Travanj_2007).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/NE_PRILAZITE_-_NA_OVOM_PODRUCJU_JE_VELIKA_OPASNOST_OD_MINA_%28Hrvatska%2C_7_Travanj_2007%29.jpg/220px-NE_PRILAZITE_-_NA_OVOM_PODRUCJU_JE_VELIKA_OPASNOST_OD_MINA_%28Hrvatska%2C_7_Travanj_2007%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/NE_PRILAZITE_-_NA_OVOM_PODRUCJU_JE_VELIKA_OPASNOST_OD_MINA_%28Hrvatska%2C_7_Travanj_2007%29.jpg/330px-NE_PRILAZITE_-_NA_OVOM_PODRUCJU_JE_VELIKA_OPASNOST_OD_MINA_%28Hrvatska%2C_7_Travanj_2007%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/NE_PRILAZITE_-_NA_OVOM_PODRUCJU_JE_VELIKA_OPASNOST_OD_MINA_%28Hrvatska%2C_7_Travanj_2007%29.jpg/440px-NE_PRILAZITE_-_NA_OVOM_PODRUCJU_JE_VELIKA_OPASNOST_OD_MINA_%28Hrvatska%2C_7_Travanj_2007%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NE_PRILAZITE_-_NA_OVOM_PODRUCJU_JE_VELIKA_OPASNOST_OD_MINA_(Hrvatska,_7_Travanj_2007).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Marking of a minefield left over from <a href="/wiki/Croatian_War_of_Independence" title="Croatian War of Independence">Croatian War of Independence</a>, typically seen in <a href="/wiki/Minefields_in_Croatia" title="Minefields in Croatia">minefields in Croatia</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Croatia, an EU member state, shares a land border with Serbia and is therefore at risk for a strong inflow of migrants from Serbia considering that <a href="/wiki/Hungary%E2%80%93Serbia_barrier" title="Hungary–Serbia barrier" class="mw-redirect">Hungary erected a fence on its border with Serbia</a>. Nearly 80% of the border consists of the Danube river, but there is a 70 kilometer-long segment of land border in <a href="/wiki/Srijem" title="Srijem" class="mw-redirect">Srijem</a>, in the forests and fields near <a href="/wiki/Tovarnik" title="Tovarnik">Tovarnik</a>. Also, parts of the Croatia-Serbia border are known minefields, which represent a considerable threat. According to the Croatian Minister of Interior <a href="/wiki/Ranko_Ostoji%C4%87" title="Ranko Ostojić">Ranko Ostojić</a>, "police in the area have enough people and equipment to protect the Croatian border against illegal immigrants".<sup id="cite_ref-auto8_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto8-126"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> Croatian President <a href="/wiki/Kolinda_Grabar-Kitarovi%C4%87" title="Kolinda Grabar-Kitarović">Kolinda Grabar-Kitarović</a> and First Deputy Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Vesna_Pusi%C4%87" title="Vesna Pusić">Vesna Pusić</a> have so far rejected the option of building a fence along the Croatian border with Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-auto9_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto9-127"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto10_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto10-128"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Croatian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Zoran_Milanovi%C4%87" title="Zoran Milanović">Zoran Milanović</a> said his country is ready to help refugees coming to Europe, insisting that people fleeing conflict should be given the right to remain in the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 15 September 2015, Croatia started to experience the first major waves of refugees of the Syrian Civil War. First Syrian refugees cross Croatia-Serbia border, carving out potential new route through Europe after Hungary seals borders.<sup id="cite_ref-aljazeera.com_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeera.com-78"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> On 15 September 2015, Hungary announced it would start arresting people crossing the border illegally, and as of early 16 September, Hungary had detained 519 people and pressed criminal charges against 46 for trespassing.<sup id="cite_ref-AlternateCroatia_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlternateCroatia-130"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> Thousands of migrants were subsequently led to pursue alternative routes through Croatia from Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-AlternateCroatia_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlternateCroatia-130"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> After Hungary closed its border with Serbia on 15 September, migrants headed towards the Serbian town of <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0id" title="Šid">Šid</a>, less than 10 kilometers from the Croatian border. Several buses filled with migrants arrived on the Croatian border crossing of <a href="/wiki/Tovarnik" title="Tovarnik">Tovarnik</a>, where the Croatian <a href="/wiki/Vukovar-Srijem_County" title="Vukovar-Srijem County">Vukovar-Srijem County</a> Care and Rescue teams as well as the <a href="/wiki/Croatian_Red_Cross" title="Croatian Red Cross">Croatian Red Cross</a> were on standby awaiting migrants.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> On 17 September, as of 3:30 AM, more than 5,000 migrants had arrived in Tovarnik.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> Interior Minister <a href="/wiki/Ranko_Ostoji%C4%87" title="Ranko Ostojić">Ranko Ostojić</a> said Croatia is "absolutely full" by the evening of 17 September 2015, and Croatia decided to close its border with Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> Train lines from Serbia via Croatia to Slovenia were closed until further notice. As of 6 October, 2015, 125,000 entered Croatia in the space of three weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> Between mid-September and mid-October 2015, about 200,000 migrants had passed through Croatia, most moving on to Hungary.<sup id="cite_ref-HungaryCroatia2_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HungaryCroatia2-124"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> On 17 October 2015, Hungary closed its border with Croatia to migrants, forcing diversion of migrants to Slovenia instead.<sup id="cite_ref-HungaryCroatia2_124-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HungaryCroatia2-124"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> However, Slovenia, with a population of only two million, stated that it would only be able to admit 2,500 people per day, stranding thousands of migrants in Croatia as well as Serbia and Macedonia, while new migrants continued to add to this backlog.<sup id="cite_ref-CroatiaSlovenia3_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CroatiaSlovenia3-135"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CroatiaSlovenia4_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CroatiaSlovenia4-136"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Slovenia">Slovenia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Slovenia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Slovenia established temporary controls on the otherwise unsupervised border with Hungary in the north east on 17 September 2015, following Germany and Austria's similar actions.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> On 18 September, Slovenia experienced first larger and largely illegal border crossing occurrences, coming mostly from Croatia, already overwhelmed by the large influx of migrant groups.</p>
<p>On the evening of 18 September, the Slovenian riot police used <a href="/wiki/Pepper_spray" title="Pepper spray">pepper spray</a> on a bridge at the <a href="/wiki/Harmica" title="Harmica">Harmica</a> border to prevent migrants and activists to cross the border from Croatia,<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>By midday of 19 September, the country registered around 1500 migrants, with all of them being accommodated in temporary reception camps or asylum centres. Largest traffic was seen at <a href="/wiki/Obre%C5%BEje,_Bre%C5%BEice" title="Obrežje, Brežice">Obrežje border crossing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dobova" title="Dobova">Dobova border crossing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bre%C5%BEice" title="Brežice">Brežice</a>. Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Miro_Cerar" title="Miro Cerar">Miro Cerar</a> visited the reception centre in Brežice on Saturday, stressing that Slovenia had the situation under control, while criticizing the Croatian government for being uncooperative.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>There were also various humanitarian and non-government organisations aiding the migrants on the border, coming mostly from Slovenia, Croatia and Austria.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 18 October 2015, Slovenia began restricting admission to 2,500 migrants per day, stranding migrants in Croatia as well as Serbia and Macedonia.<sup id="cite_ref-CroatiaSlovenia3_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CroatiaSlovenia3-135"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CroatiaSlovenia4_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CroatiaSlovenia4-136"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Austria">Austria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Austria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wien_-_V%C3%B6lkerwanderung_am_5_Sep_2015,_Westbahnhof.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Wien_-_V%C3%B6lkerwanderung_am_5_Sep_2015%2C_Westbahnhof.JPG/220px-Wien_-_V%C3%B6lkerwanderung_am_5_Sep_2015%2C_Westbahnhof.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Wien_-_V%C3%B6lkerwanderung_am_5_Sep_2015%2C_Westbahnhof.JPG/330px-Wien_-_V%C3%B6lkerwanderung_am_5_Sep_2015%2C_Westbahnhof.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Wien_-_V%C3%B6lkerwanderung_am_5_Sep_2015%2C_Westbahnhof.JPG/440px-Wien_-_V%C3%B6lkerwanderung_am_5_Sep_2015%2C_Westbahnhof.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4724" data-file-height="3150" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wien_-_V%C3%B6lkerwanderung_am_5_Sep_2015,_Westbahnhof.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Wien_Westbahnhof_railway_station" title="Wien Westbahnhof railway station">Wien Westbahnhof railway station</a> on 5 September 2015: migrants on their way to Germany</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 27 August 2015, 71 migrants were found dead in an unventilated food truck near <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>. As an official response to this tragedy, on 31 August 2015, Austria began inspections of vehicles for smuggled immigrants entering from across the border with Hungary, leading to vehicular backups of 19&#160;km (12&#160;mi) and trains stalled for hours.<sup id="cite_ref-StrainedOpenBorders_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StrainedOpenBorders-141"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Late on 4 September 2015, Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Werner_Faymann" title="Werner Faymann">Werner Faymann</a> of Austria, in conjunction with Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> of Germany, announced that migrants would be allowed to cross the border from Hungary into Austria and onward to Germany, and early on 5 September 2015, buses with migrants began crossing the Austro-Hungarian border.<sup id="cite_ref-AllowedToCross1_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AllowedToCross1-142"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AllowedToCross2_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AllowedToCross2-143"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> Austria noted that 6,500 migrants had crossed the border by the afternoon of 5 September 2015, with 2,200 already on their way to Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 14 September 2015, Austria followed Germany's suit and instituted border controls of its own at the border with Hungary.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> Austrian authorities also deployed the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Army" title="Austrian Army" class="mw-redirect">Austrian Army</a> to the border with Hungary.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 19 September 15, Austria permitted entry to approximately 10,000 migrants from Slovenia and Hungary.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> Austria has taken on the role of regulator of the flow of migrants destined for Germany by feeding, housing, and providing them health care in transit.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Polizei_f%C3%A4ngt_Fl%C3%BCchtlinge_ab.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Polizei_f%C3%A4ngt_Fl%C3%BCchtlinge_ab.jpg/220px-Polizei_f%C3%A4ngt_Fl%C3%BCchtlinge_ab.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Polizei_f%C3%A4ngt_Fl%C3%BCchtlinge_ab.jpg/330px-Polizei_f%C3%A4ngt_Fl%C3%BCchtlinge_ab.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Polizei_f%C3%A4ngt_Fl%C3%BCchtlinge_ab.jpg/440px-Polizei_f%C3%A4ngt_Fl%C3%BCchtlinge_ab.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2144" data-file-height="1600" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Polizei_f%C3%A4ngt_Fl%C3%BCchtlinge_ab.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Migrants arriving in <a href="/wiki/Munich" title="Munich">Munich</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Germany has been the most sought-after final destination in the EU migrant and refugee crisis,<sup id="cite_ref-auto6_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto6-20"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto7_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto7-21"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Thousands of migrants continued to pour into Germany from Austria as of 6 September 2015. Germany's asylum practice is to be based on article 16a of her <a href="/wiki/Basic_Law_for_the_Federal_Republic_of_Germany" title="Basic Law for the Federal Republic of Germany">Basic Law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> After the rising of the migrant crisis Germany decided to use the derogation possibility of article 17 of the <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Regulation" title="Dublin Regulation">Dublin III Regulation</a> for humanitarian reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <i>The Wall Street Journal</i>, this "<a href="/wiki/Unilateral" title="Unilateral" class="mw-redirect">unilateral</a>" open-arms policy<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> has triggered both a domestic and an international backlash.<sup id="cite_ref-BacklashGermany_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BacklashGermany-154"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> However, Germany has immediately begun to deploy a quota system to distribute asylum seekers among <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">all German states</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 2015 the federal states, responsible for accommodation, reached the brink of their capacities and criticized the Government in Berlin for its inconsiderate approach of the crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> The Interior Minister announced on 13 September the introduction of temporary controls on the southern border with Austria and explained the measure with <i>security concerns</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> The restrictions incorporated a temporary suspension of rail travel from Austria and allowed spot checks of automobiles.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> On 5 October the leading German yellow press newspaper <a href="/wiki/Bild" title="Bild">Bild</a> claimed to possess a secret document stating that the number of asylum seekers would increase to 1.5 million until the end of 2015. This report was immediately disclaimed by the German ministry of interior which restated its own estimate of 800,000 applicants "only".<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> However, chancellor <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> lost popularity because of her sentence <i>"Wir schaffen das schon"</i> (interpreted loosely as <i>"We will manage the problem with some effort"</i>), in contrast to a lot of serious problems reported from administrative institutions all over the country.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Denmark">Denmark</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Denmark">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>As of 9 September 2015, groups of migrants who declined to apply for asylum in Germany had crossed into Denmark with hopes of going to Sweden, getting into scuffles with police at a rail station in <a href="/wiki/Padborg_Station" title="Padborg Station">Padborg, Denmark</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> On 9 September, Denmark suspended all rail links with Germany and also closed a motorway on which hundreds of migrants were stopped from crossing the border.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Calais_.28France.29">Calais (France)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Calais (France)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Migrants_around_Calais" title="Migrants around Calais">Migrants around Calais</a> and <a href="/wiki/Calais_jungle" title="Calais jungle">Calais jungle</a></div>
<p>During the summer of 2015, at least nine people died in attempts to reach Britain, including falling from, or being hit by trains, and drowning in a canal at the <a href="/wiki/Eurotunnel" title="Eurotunnel">Eurotunnel</a> entrance.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Finland">Finland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Finland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Finnish press was reporting on 13 September 2015 that the local authorities had estimated the flow of 300 asylum seekers per day entering via the northern land border from Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> The total number of asylum seekers for the year was reported to be over 2.6 times the total amount for the whole of the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Russia">Russia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Russia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The number of migrants crossing from Russia into Norway increased from a handful in the first half of 2015 to 420 asylum seekers crossing by bicycle in September 2015 alone.<sup id="cite_ref-ArcticRoute_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ArcticRoute-79"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Triggers_of_the_summer_2015_crisis">Triggers of the summer 2015 crisis</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Triggers of the summer 2015 crisis">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Factors cited as immediate triggers or causes of the sudden and massive increase in migrant numbers in the summer of 2015 along the Eastern Mediterranean and Western Balkan route (Turkey-Greece-Macedonia-Serbia-Hungary) include:</p>
<ul>
<li>In mid-June 2015 the government of <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Macedonia</a> announced that it was changing its policy on migrants entering the country illegally. Previously, migrants were forbidden from transiting Macedonia, causing those who chose to do so to take perilous, clandestine modes of transit, such as walking along railroad tracks at night. Beginning in June, migrants were given three-day, temporary asylum permits, enabling them to travel by train and road.<sup id="cite_ref-MacedoniaAllows_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MacedoniaAllows-165"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EightSlyReasons_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EightSlyReasons-166"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>The opening of the Macedonia route enabled migrants from the Middle East to take very short, inexpensive voyages from the coast of Turkey to the Greek Islands, instead of the far longer, more perilous, and far more expensive voyage from Libya to Italy. According to the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Post" title="Washington Post" class="mw-redirect">Washington Post</a>, in addition to reducing the danger, this lowered the cost from $5,000 to $6,000, to $2,000 to $3,000.<sup id="cite_ref-EightSlyReasons_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EightSlyReasons-166"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>According to the Washington Post, German Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a>'s public assurance that Germany offered temporary residency to refugees combined with television footage of Germans welcoming refugees persuaded large numbers of people to migrate.<sup id="cite_ref-EightSlyReasons_166-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EightSlyReasons-166"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>The Syrian government under <a href="/wiki/Bashar_al-Assad" title="Bashar al-Assad">Bashar al-Assad</a> announced increased military conscription, and simultaneously made it easier for Syrians to obtain passports, leading Middle East policy experts to speculate that he was implementing a policy to encourage opponents of his regime to leave the country.<sup id="cite_ref-EightSlyReasons_166-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EightSlyReasons-166"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Border_crackdowns">Border crackdowns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Border crackdowns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The entry routes through the Balkans have experienced the greatest intensity of border restrictions in the 2015 EU migrant crisis, according to <i>The New York Times</i><sup id="cite_ref-BorderCrackdowns_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BorderCrackdowns-167"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> and other sources, as follows:</p>
<table class="wikitable sortable">
<tr>
<th>From</th>
<th>To</th>
<th class="unsortable">Situation</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Turkey</td>
<td>Greece</td>
<td>Greece built a razor-wire fence in 2012 along its short land border with Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-BorderCrackdowns_167-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BorderCrackdowns-167"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 2015, Turkish provincial authorities gave approximately 1,700 migrants three days to leave the border zone.<sup id="cite_ref-TurkeyGreece_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TurkeyGreece-168"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Turkey</td>
<td>Bulgaria</td>
<td>As a result of Greece's diversion of migrants to Bulgaria from Turkey, Bulgaria built its own fence to block migrants crossing from Turkey.<sup id="cite_ref-BorderCrackdowns_167-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BorderCrackdowns-167"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Greece</td>
<td>Macedonia</td>
<td>A police crackdown on migrants crossing from Greece failed in Macedonia, which therefore turned its attention instead to diverting migrants north into Serbia instead.<sup id="cite_ref-BorderCrackdowns_167-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BorderCrackdowns-167"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Serbia</td>
<td>Hungary</td>
<td>Hungary built a 175-km (109-mi) razor-wire fence along its border with Serbia in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-BorderCrackdowns_167-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BorderCrackdowns-167"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Croatia</td>
<td>Hungary</td>
<td>Hungary built a 40-km (25-mi) razor-wire fence along its border with Croatia in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-BorderCrackdowns_167-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BorderCrackdowns-167"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> On 16 October 2015, Hungary announced that it would close off its border with Croatia to migrants.<sup id="cite_ref-HungaryCroatia2_124-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HungaryCroatia2-124"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Croatia</td>
<td>Slovenia</td>
<td>Slovenia blocked transit from Croatia in September 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-BorderCrackdowns_167-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BorderCrackdowns-167"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> pepper spraying migrants trying to cross.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup> Although re-opening the border, by 18 October 2015, Slovenia restricted crossing to 2,500 migrants per day.<sup id="cite_ref-CroatiaSlovenia4_136-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CroatiaSlovenia4-136"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Hungary</td>
<td>Austria</td>
<td>Austria planned to put border controls into effect along its border with Hungary in September 2015, and officials said the controls could stay in effect under European Union rules for up to six months.<sup id="cite_ref-BorderCrackdowns_167-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BorderCrackdowns-167"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Austria</td>
<td>Germany</td>
<td>Germany placed temporary travel restrictions from Austria by rail in 2015<sup id="cite_ref-BorderCrackdowns_167-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BorderCrackdowns-167"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> but has imposed the least onerous restrictions for migrants entering by the Western Balkans route in 2015, in the context that Chancellor Angela Merkel had insisted that Europe retain open borders.<sup id="cite_ref-BorderCrackdowns_167-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BorderCrackdowns-167"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents">Incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_migrant_vessel_incidents_on_the_Mediterranean_Sea" title="List of migrant vessel incidents on the Mediterranean Sea">List of migrant vessel incidents on the Mediterranean Sea</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_migrant_vehicle_incidents_in_Europe" title="List of migrant vehicle incidents in Europe">List of migrant vehicle incidents in Europe</a></div>
<p>Several serious accidents and deaths have occurred in Europe as a result of <a href="/wiki/Migrant_smuggling" title="Migrant smuggling" class="mw-redirect">migrant smuggling</a>, both in the Mediterranean Sea, due to the capsizing of crowded and unseaworthy migrant vessels, and on European soil, due to the use of standard cargo trucks to transport migrants by smugglers.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions">Reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_Union">European Union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: European Union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the migrant shipwreck on 19 April 2015, <a href="/wiki/Italy%27s_Premier" title="Italy's Premier" class="mw-redirect">Italy's Premier</a> <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Renzi" title="Matteo Renzi">Matteo Renzi</a> spoke by telephone to French President <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Hollande" title="François Hollande">François Hollande</a> and to Maltese Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Muscat" title="Joseph Muscat">Joseph Muscat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup> They agreed to call for an emergency meeting of European interior ministers to address the problem of migrant deaths. Renzi condemned human trafficking as a "new slave trade"<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup> while Prime Minister Muscat said 19 April shipwreck was the "biggest human tragedy of the last few years". Hollande described people traffickers as "terrorists" who put migrant lives at risk. The <a href="/wiki/German_government" title="German government" class="mw-redirect">German government</a>'s representative for migration, refugees and integration, <a href="/wiki/Aydan_%C3%96zo%C4%9Fuz" title="Aydan Özoğuz">Aydan Özoğuz</a>, said that with more migrants likely to arrive as the weather turned warmer, emergency rescue missions should be restored. "It was an illusion to think that cutting off <a href="/wiki/Operation_Mare_Nostrum" title="Operation Mare Nostrum">Mare Nostrum</a> would prevent people from attempting this dangerous voyage across the Mediterranean", she said.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-175"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_175-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-175"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Federica_Mogherini" title="Federica Mogherini">Federica Mogherini</a> called for collective EU action ahead of a meeting in Luxembourg on Monday 20 April.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In a press conference, Matteo Renzi confirmed that Italy had called an "extraordinary European council" meeting as soon as possible to discuss the tragedy,<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup> various European leaders agreed with this idea.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> Cameron tweeted on 20 April that he "supported" Renzi's "call for an emergency meeting of EU leaders to find a comprehensive solution" to the migrant crisis in the Mediterranean.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup> He later confirmed that he would attend an emergency summit of European leaders on Thursday.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 20 April 2015, the European Commission proposed a 10-point plan to tackle the crisis:<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>Reinforce the Joint Operations in the Mediterranean, namely Triton and Poseidon, by increasing the financial resources and the number of assets. We will also extend their operational area, allowing us to intervene further, within the mandate of Frontex;</li>
<li>A systematic effort to capture and destroy vessels used by the smugglers. The positive results obtained with the Atalanta operation should inspire us to similar operations against smugglers in the Mediterranean;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Europol" title="Europol">Europol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frontex" title="Frontex">Frontex</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Asylum_Support_Office" title="European Asylum Support Office">EASO</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eurojust" title="Eurojust">Eurojust</a> will meet regularly and work closely to gather information on smugglers' modus operandi, to trace their funds and to assist in their investigation;</li>
<li>EASO to deploy teams in Italy and Greece for joint processing of asylum applications;</li>
<li>Member States to ensure fingerprinting of all migrants;</li>
<li>Consider options for an emergency relocation mechanism;</li>
<li>A EU wide voluntary pilot project on resettlement, offering a number of places to persons in need of protection;</li>
<li>Establish a new return programme for rapid return of irregular migrants coordinated by Frontex from frontline Member States;</li>
<li>Engagement with countries surrounding Libya through a joined effort between the Commission and the EEAS; Initiatives in Niger have to be stepped up.</li>
<li>Deploy Immigration Liaison Officers (ILO) in key third countries, to gather intelligence on migratory flows and strengthen the role of the EU Delegations.</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Border_patrol_operations">Border patrol operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Border patrol operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Operation_Triton" title="Operation Triton">Operation Triton</a> and <a href="/wiki/EU_Navfor_Med" title="EU Navfor Med">EU Navfor Med</a></div>
<p><i>The Guardian</i> and <a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a> noted that doubling the size of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Triton" title="Operation Triton">Operation Triton</a> would still leave the mission with fewer resources than the previous Italian-run rescue option (Operation Mare Nostrum) whose budget was more than 3 times as large, had 4 times the number of aircraft<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup> and had a wider mandate to conduct search and rescue operations across the Mediterranean Sea.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 23 April 2015, a five-hour emergency summit was held and EU heads of state agreed to triple the budget of Operation Triton to €120&#160;million for 2015–2016.<sup id="cite_ref-auto4_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-186"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup> EU leaders claimed that this would allow for the same operational capabilities as Operation Mare Nostrum had had in 2013–2014. As part of the agreement the United Kingdom agreed to send <a href="/wiki/HMS_Bulwark_(L15)" title="HMS Bulwark (L15)">HMS Bulwark</a>, two naval patrol boats and three helicopters to join the Operation.<sup id="cite_ref-auto4_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto4-186"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup> On 5 May 2015 it was announced by the Irish Minister of Defence <a href="/wiki/Simon_Coveney" title="Simon Coveney">Simon Coveney</a> that the <a href="/wiki/L%C3%89_Eithne_(P31)" title="LÉ Eithne (P31)">LÉ Eithne</a> would also take part in the response to the crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup> Amnesty International immediately criticized the EU response as "a face-saving not a life-saving operation" and said that "failure to extend Triton's operational area will fatally undermine today's commitment".<sup id="cite_ref-auto3_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-188"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 18 May 2015, the European Union decided to launch a new operation based in Rome, called <a href="/wiki/EU_Navfor_Med" title="EU Navfor Med">EU Navfor Med</a>, under the command of the Italian Admiral Enrico Credendino, to undertake systematic efforts to identify, capture and dispose of vessels used by migrant smugglers.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup> The first phase of the operation, launched on 22 June, involved naval surveillance to detect smugglers' boats and monitor smuggling patterns from Libya towards Italy and Malta. The second phase, called "Operation Sophia", started in October, and was aimed at disrupting the smugglers' journeys by boarding, searching, seizing and diverting migrant vessels in international waters. The operation uses six EU warships.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup> The EU seeks to increase the scope of EU Navfor Med so that a third phase of the operation would include patrols inside Libyan waters in order to capture and dispose of vessels used by smugglers.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup> Land operations on Libya to destroy vessels used by smugglers had been proposed, but commentators note that such an operation would need a UN or Libyan permit.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Relocation_and_resettlement_of_asylum_seekers">Relocation and resettlement of asylum seekers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Relocation and resettlement of asylum seekers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg/220px-European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg/330px-European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg/440px-European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="3389" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Parliament_Strasbourg_Hemicycle_-_Diliff.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> has voted in favour of a migrant quota system to make sure that <a href="/wiki/Asylum_seekers" title="Asylum seekers" class="mw-redirect">asylum seekers</a> are distributed more equally across member states.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The escalation in April 2015 of <a href="/wiki/List_of_migrant_vessel_incidents_on_the_Mediterranean_Sea" title="List of migrant vessel incidents on the Mediterranean Sea">shipwrecks of migrant boats in the Mediterranean</a> led European Union leaders to reconsider their policies on border control and processing of migrants.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup> On 20 April the European Commission proposed a 10-point plan that included the <a href="/wiki/European_Asylum_Support_Office" title="European Asylum Support Office">European Asylum Support Office</a> deploying teams in Italy and Greece for joint processing of asylum applications.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup> Also in April 2015 German chancellor <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> proposed a new system of quotas to distribute non-EU asylum seekers around the EU member states.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2015, as thousands of migrants started to move from <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">Budapest</a> to <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, Germany, Italy and France demanded asylum-seekers to be shared more evenly between EU states. Commission President <a href="/wiki/Jean-Claude_Juncker" title="Jean-Claude Juncker">Jean-Claude Juncker</a> proposed to distribute 160,000 asylum seekers among EU states under a new migrant quota system to be set out. <a href="/wiki/Jean_Asselborn" title="Jean Asselborn">Jean Asselborn</a>, the Luxembourg foreign minister, called for the establishment of a European Refugee Agency, which would have the power to investigate whether every EU member state is applying the same standards for granting asylum to migrants. Viktor Orbán, the prime minister of Hungary, criticised the European Commission warning that "tens of millions" of migrants could come to Europe. Asselborn declared to be ashamed of Orbán.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup> German Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Frank-Walter_Steinmeier" title="Frank-Walter Steinmeier">Frank-Walter Steinmeier</a> said that EU members reluctant to accept compulsory migrant quotas may have to be outvoted: "if there is no other way, then we should seriously consider to use the instrument of a qualified majority".<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Leaders of the <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group" title="Visegrád Group">Visegrád Group</a> (Czech Republic, Hungary, Poland, Slovakia) declared in a September meeting in Prague that they will not accept any compulsory long-term quota on redistribution of immigrants.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup> Czech Government Secretary for European Affairs commented that "if two or three thousand people who do not want to be here are forced into Czech Republic, it is fair to assume that they will leave anyway. The quotas are unfair to the refugees, we can't just move them here and there like a cattle." According to the Czech interior minister Milan Chovanec, from 2 September 2015, Czech Republic was offering asylum to every Syrian caught by the police notwithstanding the Dublin Regulation: out of about 1,300 apprehended until 9 September, only 60 decided to apply for asylum in Czech Republic, with the rest of them continuing to Germany or elsewhere.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup> Czech President <a href="/wiki/Milo%C5%A1_Zeman" title="Miloš Zeman">Miloš Zeman</a> said that <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukrainian</a> refugees fleeing <a href="/wiki/War_in_Donbass" title="War in Donbass">War in Donbass</a> should be also included in migrant quotas.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 7 September 2015, France announced that it would accept 24,000 asylum-seekers over two years; Britain announced that it would take in up to 20,000 refugees, primarily vulnerable children and orphans from camps in Jordan, Lebanon, and Turkey; and Germany pledged US$6.7 billion to deal with the migrant crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup> However, also on 7 September 2015, both Austria and Germany warned that they would not be able to keep up with the current pace of the influx and that it would need to slow down first.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2015-09-22_EU_JHA_Council_majority_vote_to_relocate_120,000_refugees.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/2015-09-22_EU_JHA_Council_majority_vote_to_relocate_120%2C000_refugees.svg/220px-2015-09-22_EU_JHA_Council_majority_vote_to_relocate_120%2C000_refugees.svg.png" width="220" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/2015-09-22_EU_JHA_Council_majority_vote_to_relocate_120%2C000_refugees.svg/330px-2015-09-22_EU_JHA_Council_majority_vote_to_relocate_120%2C000_refugees.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/2015-09-22_EU_JHA_Council_majority_vote_to_relocate_120%2C000_refugees.svg/440px-2015-09-22_EU_JHA_Council_majority_vote_to_relocate_120%2C000_refugees.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="702" data-file-height="675" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2015-09-22_EU_JHA_Council_majority_vote_to_relocate_120,000_refugees.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
National governments' position in the European Union Justice and Home Affairs Council majority vote to relocate 120,000 refugees:
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #8cd19d; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Yes</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff9000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Opt-out</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0000c8; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Abstention</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff0000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;No</div>
<div class="legend"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #D6D6D6; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Non-EU state</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 22 September 2015, European Union interior ministers meeting in the <a href="/wiki/Justice_and_Home_Affairs_Council" title="Justice and Home Affairs Council">Justice and Home Affairs Council</a> approved a plan to relocate 120,000 asylum seekers over two years from the frontline states <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> to all other EU countries (except Denmark, Ireland and the United Kingdom which have <a href="/wiki/Opt-outs_in_the_European_Union" title="Opt-outs in the European Union">opt-outs</a>). The relocation plan applies to asylum seekers "in clear need of international protection" (those with a recognition rate higher than 75%, i.e. <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syrians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritreans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraqis</a>) – 15,600 from Italy, 50,400 from Greece and 54,000 from Hungary – who will be distributed among EU states on the basis of quotas taking into account the size of economy and population of each state, as well as the average number of asylum applications. The decision was taken by majority vote, with the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a> voting against and <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a> abstaining. Since Hungary voted against the relocation plan, its 54,000 asylum seekers won't be relocated for now, and could be relocated from Italy and Greece instead.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> Czech Interior Minister tweeted after the vote: "Common sense lost today."<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> Slovak Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Robert_Fico" title="Robert Fico">Robert Fico</a> is threatening legal action over EU's mandatory migrant quotas at <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Justice" title="European Court of Justice">European Court of Justice</a> in Luxembourg.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup> On 9 October, the first 20 Eritrean asylum seekers were relocated by plane from Italy to Sweden,<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup> following the EU prerequisite <a href="/wiki/Fingerprinting" title="Fingerprinting" class="mw-redirect">fingerprinting</a> in Italy as the first member country of asylum registration.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="EU_.22Safe_Countries_of_Origin.22_list">EU "Safe Countries of Origin" list</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: EU &quot;Safe Countries of Origin&quot; list">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>12 EU countries already have national lists of safe countries of origin. The <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> is proposing one, common EU list designating as ‘safe’ all <a href="/wiki/EU_candidate_countries" title="EU candidate countries" class="mw-redirect">EU candidate countries</a> (<a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Former_Yugoslav_Republic_of_Macedonia" title="The Former Yugoslav Republic of Macedonia" class="mw-redirect">The Former Yugoslav Republic of Macedonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>), plus <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup> The list would allow for faster returns to those countries, even though asylum applications from nationals of those countries would continue to be assessed on an individual, case-by-case basis.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_on_Dublin_and_Schengen_rules">Effects on Dublin and Schengen rules</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Effects on Dublin and Schengen rules">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Regulation" title="Dublin Regulation">Dublin Regulation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a></div>
<p>Under the <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Regulation" title="Dublin Regulation">Dublin Regulation</a>, an asylum seeker has to apply for asylum in the first EU country they entered, and, if they cross borders to another country after being fingerprinted, they can be returned to the former. As most asylum seekers try to reach Germany or Sweden through the other EU countries in order to apply for asylum there, and as 22 EU countries form the borderless <a href="/wiki/Schengen_area" title="Schengen area" class="mw-redirect">Schengen area</a> where internal border controls are abolished, enforcement of the Dublin Regulation became increasingly difficult during late summer 2015, with some countries allowing asylum seekers to transit through their territories and other countries renouncing the right to return them back or reinstating border controls within the Schengen Area to prevent them from entering.</p>
<ul>
<li>Hungary became overburdened by asylum applications and on 23 June 2015 it stopped receiving back its applicants who later crossed the borders to other EU countries and were detained there.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On 24 August 2015, according to article 17 of the Dublin III Regulations Germany decided to suspend the general procedure as regards Syrian refugees and to process their asylum applications directly itself.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup> The change in Germany asylum policy incited large numbers of migrants to move towards Germany, especially after German chancellor Merkel stated that "there is no legal limit to refugee numbers".<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup> Austria was meanwhile allowing unimpeded travel of migrants from Hungary to Germany through its own territory.</li>
<li>On 2 September 2015, the Czech Republic also decided to defy the Dublin Regulation and to offer Syrian refugees who have already applied for asylum in other EU countries and who reach the country to either have their application processed in the Czech Republic or to continue their journey elsewhere. The rules regarding immigrants of other nationalities were not changed—i.e., they would still face detention and return under the Dublin Regulation if trying to reach Germany through the Czech Republic (unless they had the right to apply for asylum in the Czech Republic).<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On 7 September, Austria announced it will phase out special measures that have allowed tens of thousands of migrants to cross its territory and will reinstate the Dublin Regulation.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Between 9 and 10 September, Denmark closed its major motorway as well as rail lines with Germany, after hundreds of migrants refused to be registered in the country as asylum seekers and insisted to continue their travel to Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On 13 September, Germany established temporary border controls along its border with Austria, in order to "limit the current inflows" and "return to orderly procedures when people enter the country" according to German Interior Minister <a href="/wiki/Thomas_de_Maiziere" title="Thomas de Maiziere" class="mw-redirect">Thomas de Maiziere</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup> The Czech Republic reacted by increasing police presence alongside its border with Austria in order to be able to react in case the mass of migrants that was in Austria tried to reach Germany through the Czech Republic. Czech police didn't establish actual border control like Germany, but was conducting random searches of vehicles and trains within the Czech territory not far from the border, with cars and helicopters patrolling also alongside the green border. Some Czech police officers were stationed also within Austria in order to give advance warning in case large numbers of migrants would move towards the Austrian–Czech borders.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On 14 September, Austria established border controls alongside its border with Hungary. Austria deployed not only police officers, but also army along its borderline.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> Hungary also deployed army personnel along its boder with Serbia<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup> and announced that from 15 September, all persons who illegally enter the Hungarian territory of Schengen Area will be arrested and face from 3 to 5 years imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> Following Austrian chancellor Werner Faymann's remarks that Hungary's treatment of refugees is akin to Nazi policies,<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup> Hungary started transporting refugees by buses directly to the borderline with Austria, where they were offloaded and were then trying to cross to Austria on foot.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On 15 September it was reported that migrants in southern Hungary have started a hunger strike protesting the closure of the green border with Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232"><span>[</span>230<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On 16 September it was reported that Hungarian police had used tear gas and a water cannon on protesting migrants demanding the opening of the green border, after they had thrown stones and concrete at the riot police.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233"><span>[</span>231<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On 17 September, Croatia closed its border with Serbia.</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="EU_member_states">EU member states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=European_migrant_crisis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: EU member states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wien_-_Demo_Mensch_sein_in_%C3%96sterreich_-_8.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Wien_-_Demo_Mensch_sein_in_%C3%96sterreich_-_8.jpg/220px-Wien_-_Demo_Mensch_sein_in_%C3%96sterreich_-_8.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Wien_-_Demo_Mensch_sein_in_%C3%96sterreich_-_8.jpg/330px-Wien_-_Demo_Mensch_sein_in_%C3%96sterreich_-_8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Wien_-_Demo_Mensch_sein_in_%C3%96sterreich_-_8.jpg/440px-Wien_-_Demo_Mensch_sein_in_%C3%96sterreich_-_8.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="3750" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wien_-_Demo_Mensch_sein_in_%C3%96sterreich_-_8.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
'Syrian Refugees Welcome' rally in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, 31 August 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/35px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Flag_of_Austria.svg/45px-Flag_of_Austria.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span>Austria – On 6 August 2015, <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> Secretary General Heinz Patzelt inspected the refugee camp <i>Bundesbetreuungsstelle</i> in <a href="/wiki/Traiskirchen" title="Traiskirchen">Traiskirchen</a> where more than 4,800 refugees are housed while nearly 1,500 of them are sleeping outdoors. Medical expert Siroos Mirzaei from Amnesty International noted that the people had to wait for days in order to get medical help. The report also states that only four doctors are present at the refugee camp. Showers and toilets are in a dreadful condition. Mirzaei speaks about "floating excrement". According to Patzelt, "Austria is currently violating human rights and should focus on unattended children and minors".<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234"><span>[</span>232<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg/23px-Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg/35px-Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg/46px-Flag_of_Bulgaria.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span>Bulgaria – Bulgaria built a fence along its border with Turkey to prevent migrants from crossing through its territory in order to reach other EU countries. The fence is equipped with infrared cameras, motion sensors and wire, and is monitored by the army.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235"><span>[</span>233<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236"><span>[</span>234<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Croatia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Croatia.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Croatia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Croatia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Flag_of_Croatia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Croatia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span>Croatia – Croatia will receive 1,064<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237"><span>[</span>235<span>]</span></a></sup> migrants in the next two years according to the EU plan. Croatia was originally supposed to receive 505 migrants, but decided to accept more—which makes it the only country in the EU, along with Estonia, which has done so.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup> On 29 August 2015 a Croatian daily newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Jutarnji_list" title="Jutarnji list">Jutarnji list</a></i> published an interview with a "senior government official" who said that the Croatian Government formed an interdepartmental working group that is working on a plan on how to accept these migrants. Croatia will in October 2015 send its delegation to the migrants' camps in Italy and Greece, which will choose immigrants from Syria and Eritrea that Croatia will accept. Criteria for the selection will be: 1. any kind of connection to Croatia, such as family in Croatia or a diploma from one of the Croatian Universities (while Croatia was member of <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>, many foreigners from <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> countries, especially Syrians, were coming to Croatia to study), 2. education in occupations that are in demand in Croatia, and 3. families with small children.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239"><span>[</span>237<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, Croatia shares a land border with Serbia. Therefore, there is a risk of a strong inflow of migrants from Serbia considering that Hungary erected a fence on its border with Serbia. Nearly 80% of the border consists of the Danube river, but the problem is the 70 kilometers long so-called "Green Border" near <a href="/wiki/Tovarnik" title="Tovarnik">Tovarnik</a>. According to the Croatian Minister of Interior <a href="/wiki/Ranko_Ostoji%C4%87" title="Ranko Ostojić">Ranko Ostojić</a> "police in the area has enough people and equipment to protect Croatian border against illegal immigrants".<sup id="cite_ref-auto8_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto8-126"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> Croatian President <a href="/wiki/Kolinda_Grabar-Kitarovi%C4%87" title="Kolinda Grabar-Kitarović">Kolinda Grabar-Kitarović</a> and First Deputy Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Vesna_Pusi%C4%87" title="Vesna Pusić">Vesna Pusić</a> rejected the option of building a fence on Croatian border with Serbia.<sup id="cite_ref-auto9_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto9-127"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto10_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto10-128"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Grabar-Kitarović has accused German Chancellor Angela Merkel of causing "chaos".<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Anti-imigration-rally-Prague-Aug2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Anti-imigration-rally-Prague-Aug2015.jpg/220px-Anti-imigration-rally-Prague-Aug2015.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Anti-imigration-rally-Prague-Aug2015.jpg/330px-Anti-imigration-rally-Prague-Aug2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Anti-imigration-rally-Prague-Aug2015.jpg/440px-Anti-imigration-rally-Prague-Aug2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Anti-imigration-rally-Prague-Aug2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Anti-immigration rally called "For our culture and safe country" in Prague, <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a> on 12 September 2015. According to the poll, over 70% of Czechs reject migration from the Middle East and Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241"><span>[</span>239<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prorefugee_protest_Prague.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Prorefugee_protest_Prague.jpg/220px-Prorefugee_protest_Prague.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Prorefugee_protest_Prague.jpg/330px-Prorefugee_protest_Prague.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Prorefugee_protest_Prague.jpg/440px-Prorefugee_protest_Prague.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="540" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prorefugee_protest_Prague.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pro-migration rally in <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">Prague</a>, Czech Republic on 12 September 2015.</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Czech_Republic.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span>Czech Republic – Czech Republic will receive 4,306 refugees according to quotas accepted by the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242"><span>[</span>240<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="Prime Minister of the Czech Republic">Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Bohuslav_Sobotka" title="Bohuslav Sobotka">Bohuslav Sobotka</a> said the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> has failed in solving the crisis and expressed disagreement with proposed quotas saying: <i>We reject the system of quotas. I do not consider it effective, I do not think it would help bring any solution. It makes no sense to discuss any numbers for now</i>. He said Europe needs to complete what the <a href="/wiki/European_Council" title="European Council">European Council</a> has agreed in the past and not to create new plans and proposals. He supports the idea of creating hotspots in Italy or Greece.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243"><span>[</span>241<span>]</span></a></sup> Czech President <a href="/wiki/Milo%C5%A1_Zeman" title="Miloš Zeman">Miloš Zeman</a> has expressed his dissatisfaction with the mass inflow of migrants to Europe on several occasions. In late August 2015 in an interview for radio "Frekvence 1" he said: "The reception of migrants from the Middle East and Northern Africa to the territory of Czech Republic brings with it three major risks – spread of infectious diseases, terrorism of the Islamic state and the creation of new ghettos." According to his opinion the majority of refugees are actually economic migrants that are not fleeing war. The President also thinks that migrants that are crossing Czech territory in order to go to Germany will stay in Czech Republic when Germany eventually stops accepting them, "which would then make Czech Republic to defend its boundaries with the police and army".<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244"><span>[</span>242<span>]</span></a></sup> Czech Deputy Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Andrej_Babi%C5%A1" title="Andrej Babiš">Andrej Babiš</a> called for <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> intervention against human trafficking in the Mediterranean.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245"><span>[</span>243<span>]</span></a></sup> After talks with NATO Secretary General <a href="/wiki/Jens_Stoltenberg" title="Jens Stoltenberg">Jens Stoltenberg</a> on migrant crisis issue Babiš said: "NATO is not interested in refugees, though Turkey, a NATO member, is their entrance gate to Europe and smugglers operate on Turkish territory".<sup id="cite_ref-CN_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CN-246"><span>[</span>244<span>]</span></a></sup> Opposition <a href="/wiki/TOP09" title="TOP09" class="mw-redirect">TOP09</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Miroslav_Kalousek" title="Miroslav Kalousek">Miroslav Kalousek</a> said that confident and wealthy countries such as the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a> shouldn't be afraid to accept 3,000 refugees and criticised <a href="/wiki/Milo%C5%A1_Zeman" title="Miloš Zeman">President Zeman</a> of giving rise to hatred
